与其试图优化你的大脑, 让它可以管理你生活中的每一个微小细节, 不如让你的生物大脑从那份工作中解脱出来, 给它一个新的工作: 作为你生活的首席执行官, 协调和管理转变的过程信息转化为结果。我们要求你的生物大脑将记忆的工作移交给外部系统, 并通过这样做, 释放它以更具创造性的方式吸收和整合新知识。

Your Second Brain is always on, has perfect memory, and can scale to any size. The more you outsource and delegate the jobs of capturing, organizing, and distilling to technology, the more time and energy you’ll have available for the self-expression that only you can do.  
你的第二大脑始终处于开启状态, 具有完美的记忆力, 并且可以扩展到任何大小。您将捕获、组织和提炼的工作外包和委派给技术的次数越多, 您就会有更多的时间和精力用于只有您才能做到的自我表达。

Once your biology is no longer the bottleneck on your potential, you’ll be free to expand the flow of information as much as you want without drowning in it. You’ll be more balanced and peaceful, knowing you can step away from that flow at any time because it’s all being stored safely outside your head. You will be more trusting, because you’ve learned to trust a system outside yourself. It will be incredibly humbling and reassuring, in fact, that you are not solely responsible for all the remembering that needs to happen in your life. You will be more open-minded, willing to consider more unorthodox, more challenging, more unfinished ideas, because you have a plentiful supply of alternatives to choose from. You’ll want to expose yourself to more diverse perspectives, from more people, without necessarily committing to any single one. You’ll become a curator of perspectives, free to pick and choose the beliefs and concepts that serve you best in any given situation.  
一旦你的生物学不再是你潜力的瓶颈, 你就可以随心所欲地扩展信息流, 而不会淹没其中。你会更加平衡和平静, 因为你知道你可以随时远离这种流动, 因为它都安全地储存在你的头脑之外。你会更加信任他人, 因为你已经学会信任自己之外的系统。事实上, 这将令人难以置信地感到谦卑和安心, 因为您不应该独自对生活中需要发生的所有记忆负责。你的思想会更加开放, 愿意考虑更多非正统的、更具挑战性的、更多未完成的想法, 因为你有大量可供选择的选择。你会想要让自己接触更多不同的人的不同观点, 而不必只关注任何一个。您将成为观点的策展人, 可以自由挑选在任何给定情况下最适合您的信念和概念。

Delegating a job you’ve been doing for a long time is always intimidating. The voice of fear creeps up in the back of your mind: “Will there be anything left for me to do?” “Will I still be valued and needed?” We are taught that it’s better to have a secure role than risk being replaced. That it’s safer to keep your head down and not make a fuss rather than strive for something better. Emptying ourselves of our jumble of thoughts requires courage, because without our thoughts as distractions, we are left to sit with uncomfortable questions about our future and our purpose.  
委派一项你已经做了很长时间的工作总是令人生畏。恐惧的声音在你的脑海深处悄悄升起:“我还有什么可做的吗?” “我还会被重视和需要吗?” 我们被告知, 拥有一个安全的角色比冒着被替换的风险更好。保持低调而不是大惊小怪比争取更好的事情更安全。清空我们自己的杂念需要勇气, 因为如果没有我们的思想让我们分心, 我们就会坐下来思考关于我们的未来和我们的目标的令人不安的问题。

That is why building a Second Brain is a journey of personal growth. As your information environment changes, the way your mind operates starts to be transformed. You leave behind one identity and step into another—an identity as the orchestrator and conductor of your life, not its passenger. Any shift in identity can feel confronting and scary. You don’t know exactly who you will be and what it will be like on the other side, but if you persevere through the transition, there is always a new horizon of hope, possibility, and freedom waiting for you on the other side.  
这就是为什么打造第二大脑是个人成长的旅程。随着您的信息环境发生变化, 您的 mind 运作方式开始转变。你离开一个身份, 进入另一个身份——一个作为你生活的协调者和指挥者的身份, 而不是它的乘客。身份的任何转变都会让人感到对抗和恐惧。你不确切地知道你会成为什么样的人以及另一边会是什么样子, 但如果你坚持过渡, 那么在另一边总会有一个新的希望、可能性和自由的地平线在等着你。

How do you know when you’ve begun making the shift to this new identity I’ve described? The biggest shift that starts to occur as soon as you start creating a Second Brain is the shift from viewing the world through the lens of scarcity to seeing it through the lens of abundance.  
你怎么知道你什么时候开始转变为我所描述的这个新身份? 一旦你开始创造第二大脑, 最大的转变就是从稀缺的角度看世界到丰富的角度看世界。

I see so many people trying to operate in this new world under the assumptions of the past—that information is scarce, and therefore we need to acquire and consume and hoard as much of it as possible. We’ve been conditioned to view information through a consumerist lens: that more is better, without limit. Through the lens of scarcity, we constantly crave more, more, more information, a response to the fear of not having enough.[1](https://1paragraph.app/2023-02-06T09%3A26%3A12.191Z#ch10fn1) We’ve been taught that information must be jealously guarded, because someone could use it against us or steal our ideas. That our value and self-worth come from what we know and can recite on command.  
我看到很多人在过去的假设下试图在这个新世界中运作——信息是稀缺的, 因此我们需要尽可能多地获取、消费和囤积信息。我们已经习惯于通过消费主义的视角来看待信息: 越多越好, 没有限制。通过稀缺的镜头, 我们不断渴望更多、更多、更多的信息, 以回应对信息不足的恐惧。 [1](https://1paragraph.app/2023-02-06T09%3A26%3A12.191Z#ch10fn1) 我们被教导必须小心翼翼地保护信息, 因为有人可能会利用它来对付我们或窃取我们的想法。我们的价值和自我价值来自于我们所知道的并且可以根据命令背诵。

As we saw in the chapter on Capturing, the inclination to amass information can become an end in itself. It is all too easy to default to collecting more and more content without regard to whether it is useful or beneficial to us. This is indiscriminate consumption of information, treating every meme and random post on social media as if it was just as important as the most profound piece of wisdom. It is driven by fear—the fear of missing out on some crucial fact, idea, or story that everyone is talking about. The paradox of hoarding is that no matter how much we collect and accumulate, it’s never enough. The lens of scarcity also tells us that the information we already have must not be very valuable, compelling us to keep searching externally for what’s missing inside.  
正如我们在捕获一章中看到的那样, 收集信息的倾向本身可能成为目的。很容易默认收集越来越多的内容, 而不考虑它是否对我们有用或有益。这是不分青红皂白地消费信息, 将社交媒体上的每一个表情包和随机帖子都视为与最深刻的智慧一样重要。它是由恐惧驱动的——害怕错过每个人都在谈论的一些关键事实、想法或 故事。囤积的悖论是, 无论我们收集和积累多少, 都永远不够。稀缺的镜头也告诉我们, 我们已经拥有的信息一定不是很有价值, 迫使我们不断从外部寻找内部缺失的东西。

The opposite of a Scarcity Mindset is an Abundance Mindset. This is a way of looking at the world as full of valuable and helpful things—ideas, insights, tools, collaborations, opportunities. An Abundance Mindset tells us that there is an endless amount of incredibly powerful knowledge everywhere we look—in the content we consume, in our social network, in our bodies and intuitions, and in our own minds. It also tells us that we don’t need to consume or understand all of it, or even much of it. All we need is a few seeds of wisdom, and the seeds we most need tend to continually find us again and again. You don’t need to go out and hunt down insights. All you have to do is listen to what life is repeatedly trying to tell you. Life tends to surface exactly what we need to know, whether we like it or not. Like a compassionate but unyielding teacher, reality doesn’t bend or cave to our will. It patiently teaches us in what ways our thinking is not accurate, and those lessons tend to show up across our lives again and again.  
稀缺心态的对立面是丰富心态。这是一种看待世界的方式, 它充满了有价值和有用的东西——想法、见解、工具、合作、机会。丰富的心态告诉我们, 在我们所看到的任何地方——在我们消费的内容中、在我们的社交网络中、在我们的身体和直觉中, 以及在我们自己的头脑中, 都有无穷无尽的令人难以置信的强大知识。它还告诉我们, 我们不需要消费或理解所有这些, 甚至不需要大部分。我们所需要的只是一些智慧的种子, 而我们最需要的种子往往会不断地一次又一次地找到我们。您无需外出寻找见解。你所要做的就是倾听生活反复试图告诉你的事情。生活往往会准确地呈现出我们需要知道的东西, 无论我们喜欢与否。就像一位富有同情心但不屈不挠的老师, 现实不会屈服于我们的意志。它耐心地告诉我们, 我们的思维在哪些方面是不准确的, 这些教训往往会一次又一次地出现在我们的生活中。

Making the shift to a mindset of abundance is about letting go of the things we thought we needed to survive but that no longer serve us. It means giving up low-value work that gives us a false sense of security but that doesn’t call forth our highest selves. It’s about letting go of low-value information that seems important, but that doesn’t make us better people. It’s about putting down the protective shield of fear that tells us we need to protect ourselves from the opinions of others, because that same shield is keeping us from receiving the gifts they want to give us.  
转变为丰富的心态就是放弃我们认为生存所需但不再为我们服务的事物。这意味着放弃低价值的工作, 这些工作会给我们一种虚假的安全感, 但不会唤起我们最高的自我。这是关于放弃看似重要的低价值信息, 但这并不能使我们成为更好的人。这是关于放下恐惧的保护盾, 恐惧告诉我们我们需要保护自己不受他人意见的影响, 因为同样的盾牌阻止我们接受他们想要给我们的礼物。

### The Shift from Obligation to Service  
从义务到服务的转变

There is a second shift that occurs when you begin to use your Second Brain not only for remembering, but for connecting and creating. You will transition from doing things primarily out of obligation or pressure to doing things from a spirit of service.  
当你开始使用你的第二大脑不仅用于记忆, 而且用于连接和创造时, 就会发生第二次转变。您将从主要出于义务或压力而做事转变为出于服务精神而做事。

I believe most people have a natural desire within them to serve others. They want to teach, to mentor, to help, to contribute. The desire to give back is a fundamental part of what makes us human.  
我相信大多数人都有为他人服务的自然愿望。他们想要教导、指导、帮助、贡献。回馈社会的愿望是使我们成为人类的基本组成部分。

I also notice that many people put that desire on hold. They are waiting for a future time when they will have “enough” time, bandwidth, expertise, or resources. That day seems to get continuously postponed as they get new jobs, start new careers, have kids, and simply try to keep up with the demands of life.  
我还注意到许多人搁置了这种愿望。他们正在等待未来的某个时刻, 那时他们将拥有 “足够” 的时间、带宽、专业知识或资源。随着他们找到新工作、开始新的职业、生孩子, 以及只是努力跟上生活的需求, 这一天似乎不断被推迟。

You are under no obligation to help others. Sometimes it’s all you can do to take care of yourself. Still, I’ve noticed time and again a phenomenon that happens as people collect more and more knowledge in their Second Brain. That inner desire to serve slowly comes to the surface. Faced with the evidence of everything they already know, suddenly there’s no longer any reason to wait.  
您没有义务帮助他人。有时, 您所能做的就是照顾好自己。尽管如此, 我还是一次又一次地注意到随着人们在第二大脑中收集越来越多的知识而发生的一种现象。内心的服务欲望慢慢浮出水面。面对他们已知的一切证据, 突然间没有理由再等待了。

The purpose of knowledge is to be shared. What’s the point of knowing something if it doesn’t positively impact anyone, not even yourself? Learning shouldn’t be about hoarding stockpiles of knowledge like gold coins. Knowledge is the only resource that gets better and more valuable the more it multiplies. If I share a new way of thinking about your health, or finances, or business, or spirituality, that knowledge isn’t less valuable to me. It’s more valuable! Now we can speak the same language, coordinate our efforts, and share our progress in applying it. Knowledge becomes more powerful as it spreads.  
知识的目的是为了共享。如果某事对任何人都没有积极影响, 甚至对你自己都没有影响, 那么了解它又有什么意义呢? 学习不应该像金币一样囤积知识。知识是唯一的资源, 随着它的倍增, 它会变得更好、更有价值。如果我分享一种关于你的健康、财务、商业或灵性的新思考方式, 那么这些知识对我来说并没有降低价值。它更有价值! 现在我们可以说同一种语言, 协调我们的努力, 并分享我们在应用它方面的进展。知识在传播时变得更加强大。

There are problems in the world that you are uniquely equipped to solve. Problems in society like poverty, injustice, and crime. Problems in the economy like inequality, educational deficits, and workers’ rights. Problems in organizations like retention, culture, and growth. Problems in the lives of people around you that your product or service or expertise could solve, helping them communicate, learn, or work more effectively. As Ryder Carroll says in _The Bullet Journal Method_, “Your singular perspective may patch some small hole in the vast tattered fabric of humanity.”  
世界上有些问题你是独一无二的, 可以解决。社会问题, 如贫困、不公正和犯罪。经济中的问题, 如不平等、教育赤字和工人权利。组织中的问题, 如保留、文化和成长。您周围人的生活中的问题, 您的产品或服务或专业知识可以解决, 帮助他们更有效地沟通、学习或工作。正如 Ryder Carroll 在 The Bullet Journal Method 中所说,“你独特的视角可能会修补人类庞大破烂结构中的一些小洞。”

There are people who will be reached only if they are reached by you. People who have no other source for the kind of guidance you can provide. People who don’t know where to look for solutions to problems they might not even know they have. You can be that person for them. You can pay forward some of the immense care that has been poured into you by a lifetime of parents, teachers, and mentors. With mere words, you can open doors to unimaginable horizons for the people around you.  
有些人只有在您联系到他们时才能联系到他们。没有其他来源的人可以提供您可以提供的那种指导。不知道去哪里寻找问题的解决方案的人甚至可能不知道自己遇到了问题。你可以成为他们的那个人。你可以回报父母、老师和导师一生倾注的一些巨大关怀。仅仅用一句话, 你就可以为你周围的人打开通向难以想象的视野的大门。

Your Second Brain starts as a system to support you and your goals, but from there it can just as easily be used to support others and their dreams. You have everything you need to give back and be a force for good in the world. It all starts with knowledge, and you have at your disposal an embarrassment of riches.  
你的第二大脑最初是一个支持你和你的目标的系统, 但从那里它也可以很容易地用来支持他人和他们的梦想。你拥有你需要回馈的一切, 成为世界上一股向善的力量。这一切都始于知识, 而你拥有的是财富的尴尬。

The practice of building a Second Brain is more than the sum of capturing facts, theories, and the opinions of others. At its core, it is about cultivating self-awareness and self-knowledge. When you encounter an idea that resonates with you, it is because that idea reflects back to you something that is already within you. Every external idea is like a mirror, surfacing within us the truths and the stories that want to be told.  
建立第二大脑的实践不仅仅是捕捉事实、理论和他人意见的总和。它的核心是培养自我意识和自我知识。当您遇到一个与您产生共鸣的想法时, 那是因为该想法向您反映了您内在的某些东西。每一个 external 想法都像一面镜子, 在我们内心浮现出真相和想要讲述的故事。

In a 1966 book,[I](https://1paragraph.app/2023-02-06T09%3A26%3A12.191Z#footnote-001) the British-Hungarian philosopher Michael Polanyi made an observation that has since become known as “Polanyi’s Paradox.” It can be summarized as “We know more than we can say.”  
在 1966 年的一本书中, [I](https://1paragraph.app/2023-02-06T09%3A26%3A12.191Z#footnote-001) 英裔匈牙利哲学家迈克尔 · 波兰尼 (Michael Polanyi) 提出了一个后来被称为 “波兰尼悖论” 的观察结果。可以概括为“我们知道的比我们能说的更多”。

Polanyi observed that there are many tasks we can easily perform as humans that we can’t fully explain. For example, driving a car or recognizing a face. We can try to describe how we do these things, but our explanations always fall far short. That’s because we are relying on _tacit knowledge_, which is impossible to describe in exact detail. We possess that knowledge, but it resides in our subconscious and muscle memory where language cannot reach.  
Polanyi 观察到, 有许多我们作为人类可以轻松执行的任务, 但我们无法完全解释。例如, 驾驶汽车或识别人脸。我们可以尝试描述我们是如何做这些事情的, 但我们的解释总是远远不够。那是因为我们依赖于隐性知识, 这是不可能精确描述的。我们拥有这些知识, 但它存在于我们的潜意识和肌肉记忆中, 语言无法触及。

This problem—known as “self-ignorance”—has been a major roadblock in the development of artificial intelligence and other computer systems. Because we cannot describe how we know what we know, it can’t be programmed into software.  
这个被称为 “自我无知” 的问题一直是人工智能和其他计算机系统发展的主要障碍。因为我们无法描述我们如何知道我们所知道的, 所以它不能被编程到软件中。

The curse of computer scientists is our blessing, because this tacit knowledge represents the final frontier on which humans outperform machines. The jobs and endeavors that rely on tacit knowledge will be the last ones to be automated.  
计算机科学家的诅咒是我们的祝福, 因为这种隐性知识代表了人类超越机器的最终边界。依赖隐性知识的工作和努力将是最后被自动化的。

As you build your Second Brain, you will collect many facts and figures, but they are just a means to an end: discovering the tacit knowledge that lives within you. It’s in there, but you need external hooks to pull it out and into your conscious awareness. If we know more than we can say, then we need a system for continuously offloading the vast wealth of knowledge we’ve gained from real life experience.  
在构建第二大脑时, 您会收集许多事实和数据, 但它们只是达到目的的一种手段: 发现存在于您体内的隐性知识。它就在那里, 但你需要外部的钩子才能把它拉出来并进入你的意识。如果我们知道的比我们能说的多, 那么我们需要一个系统来不断卸载我们从现实生活经验中获得的大量知识。

You know things about how the world works that you can’t fully put into words. You understand human nature at a deep intuitive level. You see patterns and connections in your field that no other machine or human can see. Life has given you a set of experiences that provide you with a unique lens on the world. Through that lens you can perceive truths that can have a profoundly positive impact on you and others.  
你知道世界是如何运作的, 但你无法完全用语言表达。您以深刻的直觉 level 理解人性。您可以在您的领域中看到其他机器或人类无法看到的模式和联系。生活给了你一系列的经历, 让你以独特的视角观察世界。通过这个镜头, 您可以看到可以对您和他人产生深远积极影响的真理。

We are constantly told that we should be true to ourselves and pursue our deepest desires, but what if you don’t know what your goals and desires are? What if you have no idea what your “life purpose” is or should be? Self-direction is impossible without self-knowledge. How can you know what you want if you don’t know who you are?  
我们经常被告知我们应该忠于自己并追求我们最深切的愿望, 但是如果您不知道自己的目标和愿望是什么怎么办? 如果您不知道您的 “人生目标” 是什么或应该是什么怎么办? 没有自我知识, 自我导向是不可能的。如果你不知道自己是谁, 你怎么知道自己想要什么?

The process of knowing yourself can seem mystical, but I see it as eminently practical. It starts with noticing what resonates with you. Noticing what seems to call out to you in the external world and gives you a sense of déjà vu. There is a universe of thoughts and ideas and emotions within you. Over time, you can uncover new layers of yourself and new facets of your identity. You search outside yourself to search within yourself, knowing that everything you find has always been a part of you.  
了解自己的过程看似神秘, 但我认为它非常实用。首先要注意什么能引起你的共鸣。注意外部世界似乎在呼唤你, 让你有一种似曾相识的感觉。你内在有一个思想、想法和情感的宇宙。随着时间的推移, 您可以发现自己的新层次和身份的新方面。你向外寻找, 向内寻找, 知道你发现的一切一直都是你的一部分。

### Our Fundamental Need for Self-Expression  
我们对自我表达的基本需求

In Chapter 1, I told the story of my unexplained medical condition and how it led me to start organizing information digitally.  
在第 1 章中, 我讲述了我无法解释的身体状况以及它如何促使我开始以数字方式组织信息的故事。

There was a period a few years into that journey when I was at my lowest point. I had seemingly exhausted every avenue that modern medicine could offer me. The doctors were suggesting that it must be all in my head because their diagnostics couldn’t find anything wrong. I was in more pain than ever before, waking up with so much tension in my neck that it felt like a vise clutching me by the throat.  
在那段旅程的几年里, 我处于最低点。我似乎已经用尽了现代医学所能提供给我的所有途径。医生们暗示这一定是我脑子里的问题, 因为他们的诊断没有发现任何问题。我比以往任何时候都更痛苦, 醒来时我的脖子非常紧张, 感觉就像一把老虎钳抓住了我的喉咙。

I started withdrawing from my friends and social circles because I was so consumed by the pain I was experiencing. My attention was so focused on the pain in my body that I found it difficult to hold a conversation. I started spending more and more time by myself, on the Internet, where I could communicate and connect without speech. My view of life darkened as I slowly spiraled into depression and despair. It felt for a time like I had no future. How could I date or make friends without being able to speak? What kind of job could I hold down with unpredictable, chronic pain? What kind of future could I look forward to as my symptoms continued to worsen, without any treatment or even diagnosis on the horizon?  
我开始退出我的朋友和社交圈, 因为我被我所经历的痛苦所吞噬。我的注意力集中在我身体的疼痛上, 以至于我发现很难进行对话。我开始花越来越多的时间一个人呆在互联网上, 在那里我可以不用言语就可以交流和联系。当我慢慢陷入沮丧和绝望时, 我对生活的看法变得暗淡了。有一段时间我觉得自己没有未来。我不会说话怎么能约会或交朋友? 忍受着不可预测的慢性疼痛, 我可以从事什么样的工作? 在没有任何治疗甚至诊断的情况下, 我的症状继续恶化, 我可以期待什么样的未来?

It was around this time that I made two discoveries that changed, and saved, my life. The first was meditation and mindfulness. I began to meditate and discovered a whole realm of spirituality and introspection that I never knew existed. I learned, to my astonishment, that I am not my thoughts. That my thoughts were the constant background chatter of my subconscious mind, and that I could choose whether to “believe” what they were telling me. Meditation gave me more relief from my symptoms than anything the doctors could prescribe. My pain became my teacher, showing me what needed my attention.  
大约在这个时候, 我有了两个改变并挽救了我生命的发现。首先是冥想和正念。我开始冥想, 发现了一个我从来不知道存在的灵性和内省的整个领域。令我惊讶的是, 我了解到我不是我的想法。我的想法是我潜意识中持续不断的背景喋喋不休, 我可以选择是否 “相信” 他们告诉我的事情。冥想比医生开的任何处方都更能缓解我的症状。我的痛苦成了我的老师, 告诉我需要注意什么。

As I started having deep, profoundly moving experiences in meditation, I wanted to share what I was learning with others. This led me to my second great discovery: writing in public.[II](https://1paragraph.app/2023-02-06T09%3A26%3A12.191Z#footnote-000) I started a blog, and my very first blog post was about my experience at a Vipassana meditation retreat in Northern California. I still had trouble speaking, so writing became my refuge. On my blog, I could share anything I wanted to, in as much detail as I wanted. I was in control, with no limits on my ability to express myself.  
当我开始在冥想中获得深刻而感人的体验时, 我想与他人分享我所学到的东西。这使我有了第二个伟大发现: 公开写作。 [II](https://1paragraph.app/2023-02-06T09%3A26%3A12.191Z#footnote-000) 我开了一个博客, 我的第一篇博文是关于我在北加州内观禅修的经历。我说话还是有困难, 所以写作成了我的避难所。在我的博客上, 我可以分享我 想要的任何内容, 尽可能详细。我处于控制之中, 表达自己的能力不受限制。

I discovered something through that experience: that self-expression is a fundamental human need. Self-expression is as vital to our survival as food or shelter. We must be able to share the stories of our lives—from the small moments of what happened today at school to our grandest theories of what life is about.  
通过那次经历, 我发现了一些东西: 自我表达是人类的基本需求。自我表达对我们的生存与食物或住所一样重要。我们必须能够分享我们的生活故事——从今天在学校发生的小事到我们关于生活的最宏大理论。

### Your Turn: The Courage to Share  
轮到你了: 分享的勇气

I’ve spoken with so many people about their stories, and I’ve noticed time and again how many of them have beautiful, moving, powerful things to share. They have unique experiences that have revealed to them deep wisdom, yet they almost always undervalue those stories and experiences. They think maybe one day they’ll get around to sharing them. I’m here to tell you that there is no reason to wait. The world is desperate to hear what you know. You can change lives by sharing yourself with others.  
我和很多人谈过他们的故事, 我一次又一次地注意到他们中有多少人有美丽、感人、强大的东西可以分享。他们拥有独特的经历, 这些经历向他们揭示了深刻的智慧, 但他们几乎总是低估这些故事和经历。他们认为也许有一天他们会抽空分享它们。我在这里告诉你, 没有理由等待。世界渴望听到你所知道的。您可以通过与他人分享自己来改变生活。

It takes courage and vulnerability to stand up and deliver your message. It takes going against the grain, refusing to be quiet and hidden in the face of fear. Finding your voice and speaking your truth is a radical act of self-worth: Who are you to speak up? Who says you have anything to offer? Who are you to demand people’s attention and take up their time?  
站起来传递信息需要勇气和脆弱。它需要反其道而行之, 拒绝在恐惧面前保持安静和隐藏。找到你的声音并说出你的真相是一种自我价值的激进行为: 你是谁? 谁说你有什么可以提供的? 你是谁来引起人们的注意并占用他们的时间?

The only way to discover the answer to these questions is by speaking and seeing what comes out. Some of what you say might not resonate with others or provide value to them, but occasionally, you will strike on something—a way of seeing, a perspective, a story—that blows people’s minds and visibly transforms how they see the world. It could be someone you’re having coffee with, a client or customer, or your online followers. In those moments, the vast chasm that separates us as humans is bridged. For a brief moment, you get to feel in your bones that we are all in this together. We are all part of a vast tattered fabric of humanity, and your highest calling is simply to play your part in it.  
要找到这些问题的答案, 唯一的方法就是通过演讲和观察结果。您所说的某些内容可能不会引起其他人的共鸣或为他们提供价值, 但偶尔, 您会触及一些东西——一种看待事物的方式、一种观点、一个故事——这会打动人们的思想并明显地改变他们看待世界的方式。它可能是与您一起喝咖啡的人、客户或客户、 或您的在线粉丝。在那一刻, 将我们作为人类分开的巨大鸿沟被弥合了。有那么一瞬间, 你会从骨子里感觉到我们都在一起。我们都是人类庞大破烂结构的一部分, 您的最高使命就是在其中发挥自己的作用。

With the power of a Second Brain behind you, you can do and be anything you want. Everything is just information, and you are a master at flowing and shaping it toward whatever future you desire.  
有了第二大脑的支持, 你可以做任何你想做的事。一切都只是信息, 而你是流动和塑造它向你想要的任何未来发展的大师。

### Final Thoughts: You Can Do This  
最后的想法: 你可以做到这一点

There is no single right way to build a Second Brain. Your system can look like chaos to others, but if it brings you progress and delight, then it’s the right one.  
构建第二大脑没有唯一正确的方法。您的系统在其他人看来可能很混乱, 但如果它能给您带来进步和愉悦, 那么它就是正确的系统。

You may start with one project and slowly move on to more ambitious or complex ones as your skills develop. Or you may find yourself using your Second Brain in completely unexpected ways that you hadn’t envisioned.  
您可以从一个项目开始, 然后随着技能的发展慢慢转向更雄心勃勃或更复杂的项目。或者, 您可能会发现自己以完全出乎意料的方式使用您的第二大脑, 这是您没有预料到的。

As your needs change, give yourself the freedom to discard or take on whichever parts serve you. This isn’t a “take it or leave it” ideology where you must accept all of it or none of it. If any part doesn’t make sense or doesn’t resonate with you, put it aside. Mix and match the tools and techniques you’ve learned in this book to suit your needs. This is how you ensure your Second Brain remains a lifelong companion through the seasons of your life.  
随着您的需求发生变化, 给自己自由丢弃或接受任何适合您的部分。这不是一种 “接受或放弃” 的意识形态, 在这种意识形态中, 您必须全部接受或不接受。如果任何部分没有意义或没有引起您的共鸣, 请将其放在一边。混合搭配您在本书中学到的工具和技术以满足您的需要。这就是您如何确保您的第二大脑在您生命的各个季节都成为终生伴侣。

Wherever you are at this moment—just starting a practice to consistently take notes, or finding ways to more effectively organize and resurface your best thinking, or generating more original and impactful work—you can always fall back on the four steps of CODE:  
无论此时此刻您身在何处——只是开始练习持续记笔记, 或想方设法更有效地组织和重现您的最佳想法, 或生成更具原创性和影响力的作品——您始终可以回到 CODE 的四个步骤:

*   Keep what resonates (Capture) 保持共鸣 (捕捉)
*   Save for actionability (Organize)  
    保存可操作性 (组织)
*   Find the essence (Distill) 找到本质 (蒸馏)
*   Show your work (Express) 展示你的作品 (Express)

If at any point you feel overwhelmed, take a step back and focus on what is immediately necessary: your most important projects and priorities. Scale back to only the notes you need to move those priorities forward. Instead of trying to architect your entire Second Brain system from scratch up front, focus on moving one project at a time through each step from capturing to expressing. When you do so, you’ll find that the steps are much easier and more flexible than you imagined.  
如果您在任何时候感到不知所措, 请退后一步, 专注于立即需要的事情: 您最重要的项目和优先事项。缩小到只需要将这些优先级向前移动的注释。与其尝试从头开始构建整个 “第二大脑” 系统, 不如专注于一次完成一个项目, 完成从捕捉到表达的每一步。当你这样做的时候, 你会发现这些步骤比你想象的要简单和灵活得多。

You can also simplify things by focusing on just one stage of building your Second Brain. Think about where you are now and where you want to be in the near future:  
您还可以通过只关注构建第二大脑的一个阶段来简化事情。想想你现在在哪里, 以及你想在不久的将来去哪里:

*   Are you hoping to remember more? Focus on developing the practice of capturing and organizing your notes according to your projects, commitments, and interests using PARA.  
    你希望记住更多吗? 专注于根据使用 PARA 的项目、承诺和兴趣来记录和组织笔记。
*   Are you hoping to connect ideas and develop your ability to plan, influence, and grow in your personal and professional life? Experiment with consistently distilling and refining your notes using Progressive Summarization and revisiting them during weekly reviews.  
    您是否希望在您的个人和职业生活中联系想法并发展您的计划、影响和成长能力? 尝试使用渐进式总结不断提炼和完善您的笔记, 并在每周回顾时重新访问它们。
*   Are you committed to producing more and better output with less frustration and stress? Focus on creating one Intermediate Packet at a time and looking for opportunities to share them in ever more bold ways.  
    您是否致力于以更少的挫折和压力产生更多更好的输出? 专注于一次创建一个中间包, 并寻找机会以更大胆的方式分享它们。

As you begin your journey, here are twelve practical steps you can take right now to get your Second Brain started. Each one of them is a starting point to begin establishing the habits of personal knowledge management in your life:  
当您开始您的旅程时, 您可以立即采取以下十二个实用步骤来启动您的第二大脑。它们中的每一个都是 一个开始在你的生活中建立个人知识管理习惯的起点:

1.  **Decide what you want to capture.** Think about your Second Brain as an intimate commonplace book or journal. What do you most want to capture, learn, explore, or share? Identify two to three kinds of content that you already value to get started with.  
    确定要捕获的内容。将您的 “第二大脑” 想象成一本私密的普通书籍或期刊。您最想捕捉、学习、探索或分享什么? 确定您已经重视并开始使用的两到三种内容。
2.  **Choose your notes app.** If you don’t use a digital notes app, get started with one now. See Chapter 3 and use the free guide at [Buildingasecondbrain.com/resources](http://www.buildingasecondbrain.com/resources) for up-to-date comparisons and recommendations.  
    选择您的笔记应用程序。如果您不使用数字笔记应用程序, 请立即开始使用。请参阅第 3 章并使用 Buildingasecondbrain.com/resources 上的免费指南获取最新的比较和建议。
3.  **Choose a capture tool.** I recommend starting with a read later app to begin saving any article or other piece of online content you’re interested in for later consumption. Believe me, this one step will change the way you think about consuming content forever.  
    选择捕获工具。我建议从稍后阅读的应用程序开始, 以开始保存您感兴趣的任何文章或其他在线内容以供以后使用。相信我, 这一步将永远改变您对消费内容的看法。
4.  **Get set up with PARA.** Set up the four folders of PARA (Projects; Areas; Resources; Archives) and, with a focus on actionability, create a dedicated folder (or tag) for each of your currently active projects. Focus on capturing notes related to those projects from this point forward.  
    使用 PARA 进行设置。设置 PARA 的四个文件夹 (项目; 区域; 资源; 档案), 并以可操作性为重点, 为每个当前活动的项目创建一个专用文件夹 (或标签)。从现在开始, 专注于记录与这些项目相关的笔记。
5.  **Get inspired by identifying your twelve favorite problems.** Make a list of some of your favorite problems, save the list as a note, and revisit it any time you need ideas for what to capture. Use these open-ended questions as a filter to decide which content is worth keeping.  
    通过确定您最喜欢的十二个问题来获得灵感。列出一些您最喜欢的问题, 将列表保存为便条, 并在需要捕获什么的想法时随时重新访问它。使用这些开放式问题作为过滤器来决定哪些内容值得保留。
6.  **Automatically capture your ebook highlights.** Set up a free integration to automatically send highlights from your reading apps (such as a read later or ebook app) to your digital notes (see my recommendations at [Buildingasecondbrain.com/resources](http://www.buildingasecondbrain.com/resources)).  
    自动捕捉您的电子书亮点。设置免费集成, 自动将阅读应用程序 (例如稍后阅读或电子书应用程序) 中的精彩内容发送到数字 notes(请参阅我在 Buildingasecondbrain.com/resources 上的建议)。
7.  **Practice Progressive Summarization.** Summarize a group of notes related to a project you’re currently working on using multiple layers of highlighting to see how it affects the way you interact with those notes.  
    练习渐进式总结。总结一组与您当前正在处理的项目相关的笔记, 使用多层突出显示来查看它如何影响您与这些笔记交互的方式。
8.  **Experiment with just one Intermediate Packet.** Choose a project that might be vague, sprawling, or simply hard, and pick just _one_ piece of it to work on—an Intermediate Packet. Maybe it is a business proposal, a chart, a run of show for an event, or key topics for a meeting with your boss. Break the project down into smaller pieces, make a first pass at one of the pieces, and share it with at least one person to get feedback.  
    只用一个中间数据包进行试验。选择一个可能模糊、庞大或简单困难的项目, 然后只选择其中的一部分来处理——一个中间包。也许它是一份商业计划书、一张图表、一场活动的演出, 或者是与老板会面的关键话题。将项目分解成更小的部分, 对其中一个部分进行第一次检查, 并与至少一个人分享以获得反馈。
9.  **Make progress on one deliverable.** Choose a project deliverable you’re responsible for and, using the Express techniques of Archipelago of Ideas, Hemingway Bridge, and Dial Down the Scope, see if you can make decisive progress on it using only the notes in your Second Brain.  
    在一项可交付成果上取得进展。选择一个你负责的项目可交付成果, 并使用 Archipelago of Ideas、Hemingway Bridge 和 Dial Down the Scope 的快速表达技术, 看看你是否可以仅使用第二大脑中的笔记就可以取得决定性的进展。
10.  **Schedule a Weekly Review.** Put a weekly recurring meeting with yourself on your calendar to begin establishing the habit of conducting a Weekly Review. To start, just clear your notes inbox and decide on your priorities for the week. From there, you can add other steps as your confidence grows.  
    安排每周回顾。将每周与自己的定期会议记在日历上, 开始养成进行每周回顾的习惯。首先, 只需清除您的笔记收件箱并确定本周的优先事项。随着信心的增强, 您可以从那里添加其他步骤。
11.  **Assess your notetaking proficiency.** Evaluate your current notetaking practices and areas for potential improvement using our free assessment tool at [Buildingasecondbrain.com/quiz](http://www.buildingasecondbrain.com/quiz).  
    评估你的笔记能力。使用我们位于 Buildingasecondbrain.com/quiz 的免费评估工具, 评估您当前的记笔记做法和可能改进的领域。
12.  **Join the PKM community.** On Twitter, LinkedIn, Substack, Medium, or your platform(s) of choice, follow and subscribe to thought leaders and join communities who are creating content related to personal knowledge management (#PKM), #SecondBrain, #BASB, or #toolsforthought. Share your top takeaways from this book or anything else you’ve realized or discovered. There’s nothing more effective for adopting new behaviors than surrounding yourself with people who already have them.  
    加入 PKM 社区。在 Twitter、LinkedIn、Substack、Medium 或您选择的平台上, 关注并订阅思想领袖并加入创建与个人知识管理 (#PKM)、#SecondBrain、#BASB 或 #toolsforthought 相关内容的社区. 分享您从这本书或您意识到或发现的任何其他事情中获得的最重要的 takeaways。没有什么比与已经拥有这些行为的人在一起更有效地采用新行为了。

While building a Second Brain is a project—something you can commit to and achieve within a reasonable period of time—_using_ your Second Brain is a lifelong practice. I recommend you revisit _Building a Second Brain_ at various points over time. I guarantee you’ll notice things you missed the first time.  
虽然构建第二大脑是一个项目——你可以在合理的时间内致力于并实现的项目——但使用你的第二大脑是一项终身实践。我建议您随着时间的推移在不同的时间点重新访问构建第二个大脑。我保证你会注意到你第一次错过的事情。

Whether you focus on implementing one aspect of the CODE Method, make a full commitment to the entire process, or something in between, you are taking on a new relationship with the information in your life. You are developing a new relationship to your own attention and energy. You are committing to a new identity in which you are in charge of the information swirling around you, even if you don’t always know what it means.  
无论您专注于实施 CODE 方法的一个方面, 对整个过程做出全面承诺, 还是介于两者之间, 您都在与生活中的信息建立一种新的关系。您正在与自己的注意力和精力建立新的关系。你正在致力于一个新的身份, 在这个身份中你负责在你周围盘旋的信息, 即使你并不总是知道它意味着什么。

As you embark on the lifelong path of personal knowledge management, remember that you’ve achieved success before. There have been practices that you’d never heard of before, that are now integral parts of your life. There have been habits and skills that seemed impossible to master, that you now can’t imagine living without. There have been new technologies that you swore you would never embrace that you now use every day. This is the same—what seems unfamiliar and strange now will eventually feel completely natural.  
当您踏上个人知识管理的终生之路时, 请记住您以前取得过成功。有一些您以前从未听说过的做法, 现在已成为您生活中不可或缺的一部分。有些习惯和技能似乎无法掌握, 你现在无法想象没有它们的生活。有一些你发誓永远不会接受的新技术, 但你现在每天都在使用。这是一样的——现在看起来陌生和陌生的东西最终会变得完全自然。

If I could leave you with one last bit of advice, it is to chase what excites you. When you are captivated and obsessed by a story, an idea, or a new possibility, don’t just let that moment pass as if it doesn’t matter. Those are the moments that are truly precious, and that no technology can produce for you. Run after your obsessions with everything you have.  
如果我能给你最后一点建议, 那就是去追逐让你兴奋的事情。当你被一个故事、一个想法或一个新的可能性所吸引和着迷时, 不要让那一刻过去, 就好像它无关紧要一样。那些是真正珍贵的时刻, 任何技术都无法为您呈现。追逐你所拥有的一切。

Just be sure to take notes along the way.  
请务必在整个过程中做笔记。

1.  [II](https://1paragraph.app/2023-02-06T09%3A26%3A12.191Z#footnote-000-backlink). I came to appreciate the incredible power of writing in public through my partnership with David Perell, who teaches people how to do it via his online writing school Write of Passage, which you can learn more about at [writeofpassage.school](http://writeofpassage.school/).  
    二。通过与 David Perell 的合作, 我开始欣赏公开写作的不可思议的力量, 他通过他的在线写作学校 Write of Passage 教人们如何做到这一点, 您可以在 writeofpassage.school 了解更多信息。

Bonus Chapter How to Create a Tagging System That Works  
奖金章节 如何创建有效的标记系统
--------------------------------------------------------------------------

I wrote this book to give you a new way to think about the knowledge that matters to you. It’s designed to give anyone a path to create—and benefit from—a Second Brain and provides an introduction to the fascinating world of personal knowledge management.  
我写这本书是为了给你一种新的方式来思考对你重要的知识。它旨在为任何人提供创建第二大脑并从中受益的途径, 并介绍个人知识管理的迷人世界。

The practice begins and ends with notetaking—including capturing, organizing, distilling, and expressing information, ideas, and packets of work. The specific techniques in the CODE chapters are the best place to get started. However, one of the most common questions I receive is about the advanced skill of tagging.  
练习以记笔记开始和结束——包括捕捉、组织、提炼和表达信息、想法和工作包。 CODE 章节中的特定技术是入门的最佳起点。但是, 我收到的最常见问题之一是关于标记的高级技能。

I’ve compiled a bonus chapter on how to create a tagging system for your Second Brain following the principle of actionability. Although not essential for getting started, tags do provide an extra layer of organization that can be useful as your knowledge collection grows.  
我编写了一个额外的章节, 介绍如何根据可操作性原则为您的第二大脑创建标记系统。虽然对于入门来说不是必需的, 但标签确实提供了一个额外的组织层, 随着您的知识收集的增长, 它会很有用。

You can download this chapter at [Buildingasecondbrain.com/bonuschapter](http://www.buildingasecondbrain.com/bonuschapter).  
您可以在 Buildingasecondbrain.com/bonuschapter 下载本章。

Additional Resources and Guidelines  
其他资源和指南
---------------------------------------------

The technology landscape is constantly changing, and the best practices evolve as new platforms emerge. I’ve created the Second Brain Resource Guide as a public resource with continually updated recommendations for the best notes apps, capture tools and other useful apps, frequently asked questions, and other advice and guidelines to help you succeed in personal knowledge management. You can access it at [https://www.buildingasecondbrain.com/resources](https://www.buildingasecondbrain.com/resources).  
技术格局在不断变化, 最佳实践随着新平台的出现而发展。我创建了第二大脑资源指南作为公共资源, 不断更新最佳笔记应用程序、捕获工具和其他有用应用程序的建议、常见问题以及其他建议和指南, 以帮助您在个人知识管理方面取得成功。您可以在 [https://www.buildingasecondbrain.com/resources](https://www.buildingasecondbrain.com/resources) 访问它。

You are the ultimate authority on what works and what doesn’t. 我的一切最终都来自我的家庭。我的土壤和我的岩石, 我生命中的意义和快乐从中涌现。感谢我的父母 Wayne Forte 和 Valeria Vassão Forte, 是他们在我的成长过程中让我接触到无数丰富的经历、文化、地方和人物。爸爸, 您是我的榜样, 体现了以毫不留情的诚实和品味表达自己的意义, 同时也履行了我作为父亲、丈夫和公民的责任。妈妈, 您给了我天赋来平衡我坚强的意志和尖锐的舌头——耐心、慷慨、仁慈和自我意识。你们俩都献出了自己的生命, 让我成为可以与他人分享的富足之人。本书中表达的许多教义都源于您在孩提时教给我并为我树立榜样的简单、实用的课程。致我的兄弟姐妹和姻亲 Lucas、Paloma、Marco、Kaitlyn 和 Grant。你们是我最好的朋友, 我的知己, 我一生的伴侣。每当我开始忘记我是谁, 什么对我重要时, 你就会把我带回我的故乡。我珍惜我们一起度过的每一分钟。

You became whoever you needed to become, acquired whichever skills were demanded of you, and ventured into one new territory after another, all to help me reach my dreams. There’s nothing more gratifying in my life than watching you grow and evolve into the most inspiring, genuine, open-hearted person I’ve ever met. I consider it my highest privilege to walk alongside you as you step into your greatness. Caio, you’ve only just arrived, but already I can’t live without you. CHAPTER 4: CAPTURE—KEEP WHAT RESONATES  
第 4 章: 捕捉——保持共鸣
